The Gulf Stream also keeps extreme temperatures from occurring on the Florida Peninsula. In the higher latitudes, the North Atlantic Drift, warms the atmosphere over the oceans, keeping the British Isles and north-western Europe mild and cloudy, and not severely cold in winter like other locations at the same high latitude. The cold water currents contribute to heavy fog off the coast of eastern Canada (the\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Banks_of_Newfoundland" title="Grand Banks of Newfoundland">\n        Grand Banks of Newfoundland\n       </a>\n       area) and Africa\'s north-western coast. In general, winds transport moisture and air over land areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USN-2001_5-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USN-2001-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_hazards">\n        Natural hazards\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Natural hazards">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iceberg_A22A,_South_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg">\n         <img alt="Overhead photo of iceberg" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1553" data-file-width="2345" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Iceberg_A22A%2C_South_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/220px-Iceberg_A22A%2C_South_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Iceberg_A22A%2C_South_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/330px-Iceberg_A22A%2C_South_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Iceberg_A22A%2C_South_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/440px-Iceberg_A22A%2C_South_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iceberg_A22A,_South_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Iceberg A22A in the South Atlantic Ocean\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Iceberg" title="Iceberg">\n        Icebergs\n       </a>\n       are common from February to August in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Davis_Strait" title="Davis Strait">\n        Davis Strait\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Denmark_Strait" title="Denmark Strait">\n        Denmark Strait\n       </a>\n       , and the northwestern Atlantic and have been spotted as far south as\n       <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">\n        Bermuda\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">\n        Madeira\n       </a>\n       . Ships are subject to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superstructure_(ship)" title="Superstructure (ship)">\n        superstructure\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Icing_(nautical)" title="Icing (nautical)">\n        icing\n       </a>\n       in the extreme north from October to May. Persistent fog can be a maritime hazard from May to September, as can hurricanes north of the equator (May to December).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The United States\' southeast coast, especially the Virginia and North Carolina coasts, has a long history of shipwrecks due to its many shoals and reefs.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Triangle" title="Bermuda Triangle">\n        Bermuda Triangle\n       </a>\n       is popularly believed to be the site of numerous aviation and shipping incidents because of unexplained and supposedly mysterious causes, but\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coast_Guard" title="Coast Guard">\n        Coast Guard\n       </a>\n       records do not support this belief.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricanes" title="Hurricanes">\n        Hurricanes\n       </a>\n       are also a natural hazard in the Atlantic, but mainly in the northern part of the ocean, rarely\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclones" title="Tropical cyclones">\n        tropical cyclones\n       </a>\n       form in the southern parts. Hurricanes usually form annually between June and November.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plate_tectonics">\n        Plate tectonics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Plate tectonics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pangea_animation_03.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="200" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8e/Pangea_animation_03.gif" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pangea_animation_03.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The break-up of Pangaea resulted in the opening of the Atlantic Ocean in three stages\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Atlantic">\n        Central Atlantic\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Central Atlantic">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The break-up of Pangaea began in the Central Atlantic, between North America and Northwest Africa, where rift basins opened during the Late Triassic and Early Jurassic. This period also saw the first stages of the uplift of the Atlas Mountains. The exact timing is controversial with estimates ranging from 200 to 170\xc2\xa0Ma.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The opening of the Atlantic Ocean coincided with the initial break-up of the supercontinent\n       <a href="/wiki/Pangaea" title="Pangaea">\n        Pangaea\n       </a>\n       , both of which were initiated by the eruption of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Atlantic_Magmatic_Province" title="Central Atlantic Magmatic Province">\n        Central Atlantic Magmatic Province\n       </a>\n       (CAMP), one of the most extensive and voluminous\n       <a href="/wiki/Large_igneous_province" title="Large igneous province">\n        large igneous provinces\n       </a>\n       in Earth\'s history associated with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Triassic%E2%80%93Jurassic_extinction_event" title="Triassic\xe2\x80\x93Jurassic extinction event">\n        Triassic\xe2\x80\x93Jurassic extinction event\n       </a>\n       , one of Earth\'s major\n       <a href="/wiki/Extinction_event" title="Extinction event">\n        extinction events\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Theoliitic\n       <a href="/wiki/Dike_(geology)" title="Dike (geology)">\n        dikes\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Aquatic_sill" title="Aquatic sill">\n        sills\n       </a>\n       , and lava flows from the CAMP eruption at 200\xc2\xa0Ma have been found in West Africa, eastern North America, and northern South America. The extent of the volcanism has been estimated to 4.5\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        6\n       </sup>\n       km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       (1.7\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        6\n       </sup>\n       sq\xc2\xa0mi) of which 2.5\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        6\n       </sup>\n       km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       (9.7\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        5\n       </sup>\n       sq\xc2\xa0mi) covered what is now northern and central Brazil.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The formation of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Isthmus" title="Central American Isthmus">\n        Central American Isthmus\n       </a>\n       closed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Seaway" title="Central American Seaway">\n        Central American Seaway\n       </a>\n       at the end of the Pliocene 2.8\xc2\xa0Ma ago. The formation of the isthmus resulted in the migration and extinction of many land-living animals, known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_American_Interchange" title="Great American Interchange">\n        Great American Interchange\n       </a>\n       , but the closure of the seaway resulted in a "Great American Schism" as it affected ocean currents, salinity, and temperatures in both the Atlantic and Pacific. Marine organisms on both sides of the isthmus became isolated and either diverged or went extinct.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Atlantic">\n        <span id="NORTH_ATLANTIC">\n        </span>\n        <span id="Northern_Atlantic">\n         Northern Atlantic\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Northern Atlantic">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Opening_of_the_North_Atlantic_Ocean" title="Opening of the North Atlantic Ocean">\n        Opening of the North Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Geologically the Northern Atlantic is the area delimited to the south by two conjugate margins, Newfoundland and Iberia, and to the north by the Arctic\n       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Basin" title="Eurasian Basin">\n        Eurasian Basin\n       </a>\n       . The opening of the Northern Atlantic closely followed the margins of its predecessor, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Iapetus_Ocean" title="Iapetus Ocean">\n        Iapetus Ocean\n       </a>\n       , and spread from the Central Atlantic in six stages:\n       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">\n        Iberia\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93\n       <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">\n        Newfoundland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Porcupine_Bank" title="Porcupine Bank">\n        Porcupine\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93North America, Eurasia\xe2\x80\x93Greenland, Eurasia\xe2\x80\x93North America. Active and inactive spreading systems in this area are marked by the interaction with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Iceland_hotspot" title="Iceland hotspot">\n        Iceland hotspot\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="South_Atlantic">\n        South Atlantic\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: South Atlantic">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       West Gondwana (South America and Africa) broke up in the Early Cretaceous to form the South Atlantic. The apparent fit between the coastlines of the two continents was noted on the first maps that included the South Atlantic and it was also the subject of the first computer-assisted plate tectonic reconstructions in 1965.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eagles-intro_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Eagles-intro-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This magnificent fit, however, has since then proven problematic and later reconstructions have introduced various deformation zones along the shorelines to accommodate the northward-propagating break-up.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eagles-intro_43-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Eagles-intro-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Intra-continental rifts and deformations have also been introduced to subdivide both continental plates into sub-plates.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seton-2012-p217_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Seton-2012-p217-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Geologically the South Atlantic can be divided into four segments: Equatorial segment, from 10\xc2\xb0N to the Romanche Fracture Zone (RFZ);; Central segment, from RFZ to Florianopolis Fracture Zone (FFZ, north of Walvis Ridge and Rio Grande Rise); Southern segment, from FFZ to the Agulhas-Falkland Fracture Zone (AFFZ); and Falkland segment, south of AFFZ.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Torsvik2009-p1316_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Torsvik2009-p1316-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the southern segment the Early Cretaceous (133\xe2\x80\x93130\xc2\xa0Ma) intensive magmatism of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_and_Etendeka_traps" title="Paran\xc3\xa1 and Etendeka traps">\n        Paran\xc3\xa1\xe2\x80\x93Etendeka Large Igneous Province\n       </a>\n       produced by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tristan_hotspot" title="Tristan hotspot">\n        Tristan hotspot\n       </a>\n       resulted in an estimated volume of 1.5\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        6\n       </sup>\n       to 2.0\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        6\n       </sup>\n       km\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       (3.6\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        5\n       </sup>\n       to 4.8\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        5\n       </sup>\n       cu\xc2\xa0mi). It covered an area of 1.2\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        6\n       </sup>\n       to 1.6\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        6\n       </sup>\n       km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       (4.6\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        5\n       </sup>\n       to 6.2\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        5\n       </sup>\n       sq\xc2\xa0mi) in Brazil, Paraguay, and Uruguay and 0.8\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        5\n       </sup>\n       km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       (3.1\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        4\n       </sup>\n       sq\xc2\xa0mi) in Africa.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dyke_swarm" title="Dyke swarm">\n        Dyke swarms\n       </a>\n       in Brazil, Angola, eastern Paraguay, and Namibia, however, suggest the LIP originally covered a much larger area and also indicate failed rifts in all these areas. Associated offshore basaltic flows reach as far south as the Falkland Islands and South Africa. Traces of magmatism in both offshore and onshore basins in the central and southern segments have been dated to 147\xe2\x80\x9349\xc2\xa0Ma with two peaks between 143\xe2\x80\x93121\xc2\xa0Ma and 90\xe2\x80\x9360\xc2\xa0Ma.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Torsvik2009-p1316_46-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Torsvik2009-p1316-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the Falkland segment rifting began with dextral movements between the Patagonia and Colorado sub-plates between the Early Jurassic (190\xc2\xa0Ma) and the Early Cretaceous (126.7\xc2\xa0Ma). Around 150\xc2\xa0Ma sea-floor spreading propagated northward into the southern segment. No later than 130\xc2\xa0Ma rifting had reached the Walvis Ridge\xe2\x80\x93Rio Grande Rise.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seton-2012-p217_45-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Seton-2012-p217-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the central segment rifting started to break Africa in two by opening the\n       <a href="/wiki/Benue_Trough" title="Benue Trough">\n        Benue Trough\n       </a>\n       around 118\xc2\xa0Ma. Rifting in the central segment, however, coincided with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Geomagnetic_reversal#Superchrons" title="Geomagnetic reversal">\n        Cretaceous Normal Superchron\n       </a>\n       (also known as the Cretaceous quiet period), a 40\xc2\xa0Ma period without magnetic reversals, which makes it difficult to date sea-floor spreading in this segment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seton-2012-p217_45-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Seton-2012-p217-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The equatorial segment is the last phase of the break-up, but, because it is located on the Equator, magnetic anomalies cannot be used for dating. Various estimates date the propagation of sea-floor spreading in this segment to the period 120\xe2\x80\x9396\xc2\xa0Ma. This final stage, nevertheless, coincided with or resulted in the end of continental extension in Africa.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seton-2012-p217_45-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Seton-2012-p217-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       About 50\xc2\xa0Ma the opening of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Drake_Passage" title="Drake Passage">\n        Drake Passage\n       </a>\n       resulted from a change in the motions and separation rate of the South American and Antarctic plates. First small ocean basins opened and a shallow gateway appeared during the Middle Eocene. 34\xe2\x80\x9330\xc2\xa0Ma a deeper seaway developed, followed by an\n       <a href="/wiki/Eocene%E2%80%93Oligocene_extinction_event" title="Eocene\xe2\x80\x93Oligocene extinction event">\n        Eocene\xe2\x80\x93Oligocene climatic deterioration\n       </a>\n       and the growth of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_ice_sheet" title="Antarctic ice sheet">\n        Antarctic ice sheet\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Closure_of_the_Atlantic">\n        Closure of the Atlantic\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Closure of the Atlantic">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Pangaea_Ultima" title="Pangaea Ultima">\n        Pangaea Ultima\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       An embryonic subduction margin is potentially developing west of Gibraltar. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Arc" title="Gibraltar Arc">\n        Gibraltar Arc\n       </a>\n       in the western Mediterranean is migrating westward into the Central Atlantic where it joins the converging African and Eurasian plates. Together these three tectonic forces are slowly developing into a new subduction system in the eastern Atlantic Basin. Meanwhile, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Scotia_Arc" title="Scotia Arc">\n        Scotia Arc\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">\n        Caribbean Plate\n       </a>\n       in the western Atlantic Basin are eastward-propagating subduction systems that might, together with the Gibraltar system, represent the beginning of the closure of the Atlantic Ocean and the final stage of the Atlantic\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilson_Cycle" title="Wilson Cycle">\n        Wilson Cycle\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main category:\n       <a href="/wiki/Category:History_of_the_Atlantic_Ocean" title="Category:History of the Atlantic Ocean">\n        History of the Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Human_origin">\n        Human origin\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Human origin">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_evolution" title="Human evolution">\n        Humans evolved\n       </a>\n       in Africa; first by diverging from other apes around 7\xc2\xa0Ma; then developing stone tools around 2.6\xc2\xa0Ma; to finally evolve as\n       <a href="/wiki/Anatomically_modern_human" title="Anatomically modern human">\n        modern humans\n       </a>\n       around 100\xc2\xa0kya. The earliest evidences for the complex behavior associated with this\n       <a href="/wiki/Behavioral_modernity" title="Behavioral modernity">\n        behavioral modernity\n       </a>\n       has been found in the Greater\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Floristic_Region" title="Cape Floristic Region">\n        Cape Floristic Region\n       </a>\n       (GCFR) along the coast of South Africa. During the latest glacial stages the now-submerged plains of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Agulhas_Bank" title="Agulhas Bank">\n        Agulhas Bank\n       </a>\n       were exposed above sea level, extending the South African coastline farther south by hundreds of kilometers. A small population of modern humans\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 probably fewer than a thousand reproducing individuals\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 survived glacial maxima by exploring the high diversity offered by these Palaeo-Agulhas plains. The GCFR is delimited to the north by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Fold_Belt" title="Cape Fold Belt">\n        Cape Fold Belt\n       </a>\n       and the limited space south of it resulted in the development of social networks out of which complex Stone Age technologies emerged.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Human history thus begins on the coasts of South Africa where the Atlantic\n       <a href="/wiki/Benguela_Current" title="Benguela Current">\n        Benguela Upwelling\n       </a>\n       and Indian Ocean\n       <a href="/wiki/Agulhas_Current" title="Agulhas Current">\n        Agulhas Current\n       </a>\n       meet to produce an intertidal zone on which shellfish, fur seal, fishes and sea birds provided the necessary protein sources.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The African origin of this modern behaviour is evidenced by 70,000 years-old engravings from\n       <a href="/wiki/Blombos_Cave" title="Blombos Cave">\n        Blombos Cave\n       </a>\n       , South Africa.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Old_World">\n        Old World\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Old World">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrial_DNA" title="Mitochondrial DNA">\n        Mitochondrial DNA\n       </a>\n       (mtDNA) studies indicate that 80\xe2\x80\x9360,000 years ago a major demographic expansion within Africa, derived from a single, small population, coincided with the emergence of behavioral complexity and the rapid\n       <a href="/wiki/Marine_isotope_stage" title="Marine isotope stage">\n        MIS\n       </a>\n       5\xe2\x80\x934 environmental changes. This group of people not only expanded over the whole of Africa, but also started to disperse\n       <a href="/wiki/Recent_African_origin_of_modern_humans" title="Recent African origin of modern humans">\n        out of Africa\n       </a>\n       into Asia, Europe, and Australasia around 65,000 years ago and quickly replaced the archaic humans in these regions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During the\n       <a href="/wiki/Last_Glacial_Maximum" title="Last Glacial Maximum">\n        Last Glacial Maximum\n       </a>\n       (LGM) 20,000 years ago humans had to abandon their initial settlements along the European North Atlantic coast and retreat to the Mediterranean. Following rapid climate changes at the end of the LGM this region was repopulated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Magdalenian" title="Magdalenian">\n        Magdalenian\n       </a>\n       culture. Other hunter-gatherers followed in waves interrupted by large-scale hazards such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Laacher_See" title="Laacher See">\n        Laacher See\n       </a>\n       volcanic eruption, the inundation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Doggerland" title="Doggerland">\n        Doggerland\n       </a>\n       (now the\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">\n        North Sea\n       </a>\n       ), and the formation of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">\n        Baltic Sea\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The European coasts of the North Atlantic were permanently populated about 9\xe2\x80\x938.5 thousand years ago.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This human dispersal left abundant traces along the coasts of the Atlantic Ocean. 50\xc2\xa0ka-old, deeply stratified\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shell_midden" title="Shell midden">\n        shell middens\n       </a>\n       found in\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ysterfontein&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ysterfontein (page does not exist)">\n        Ysterfontein\n       </a>\n       on the western coast of South Africa are associated with the Middle Stone Age (MSA). The MSA population was small and dispersed and the rate of their reproduction and exploitation was less intense than those of later generations. While their middens resemble 12\xe2\x80\x9311\xc2\xa0ka-old Late Stone Age (LSA) middens found on every inhabited continent, the 50\xe2\x80\x9345\xc2\xa0ka-old\n       <a href="/wiki/Enkapune_Ya_Muto" title="Enkapune Ya Muto">\n        Enkapune Ya Muto\n       </a>\n       in Kenya probably represents the oldest traces of the first modern humans to disperse out of Africa.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meilgaard-boplads.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="353" data-file-width="500" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Meilgaard-boplads.jpg/220px-Meilgaard-boplads.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Meilgaard-boplads.jpg/330px-Meilgaard-boplads.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Meilgaard-boplads.jpg/440px-Meilgaard-boplads.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meilgaard-boplads.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Excavation of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Erteb%C3%B8lle_culture" title="Erteb\xc3\xb8lle culture">\n          Erteb\xc3\xb8lle\n         </a>\n         middens in 1880\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The same development can be seen in Europe. In\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_Riera_Cave&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La Riera Cave (page does not exist)">\n        La Riera Cave\n       </a>\n       (23\xe2\x80\x9313\xc2\xa0ka) in Asturias, Spain, only some 26,600 molluscs were deposited over 10\xc2\xa0ka. In contrast, 8\xe2\x80\x937\xc2\xa0ka-old shell middens in Portugal, Denmark, and Brazil generated thousands of tons of debris and artefacts. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Erteb%C3%B8lle_culture" title="Erteb\xc3\xb8lle culture">\n        Erteb\xc3\xb8lle\n       </a>\n       middens in Denmark, for example, accumulated 2,000\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       (71,000\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0ft) of shell deposits representing some 50 million molluscs over only a thousand years. This intensification in the exploitation of marine resources has been described as accompanied by new technologies\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 such as boats, harpoons, and fish-hooks\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 because many caves found in the Mediterranean and on the European Atlantic coast have increased quantities of marine shells in their upper levels and reduced quantities in their lower. The earliest exploitation, however, took place on the now submerged shelves, and most settlements now excavated were then located several kilometers from these shelves. The reduced quantities of shells in the lower levels can represent the few shells that were exported inland.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="New_World">\n        New World\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: New World">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       During the LGM the\n       <a href="/wiki/Laurentide_Ice_Sheet" title="Laurentide Ice Sheet">\n        Laurentide Ice Sheet\n       </a>\n       covered most of northern North America while\n       <a href="/wiki/Beringia" title="Beringia">\n        Beringia\n       </a>\n       connected Siberia to Alaska. In 1973 late U.S. geoscientist\n       <a href="/wiki/Paul_S._Martin" title="Paul S. Martin">\n        Paul S. Martin\n       </a>\n       proposed a "blitzkrieg" colonization of America by which\n       <a href="/wiki/Clovis_culture" title="Clovis culture">\n        Clovis hunters\n       </a>\n       migrated into North America around 13,000 years ago in a single wave through an ice-free corridor in the ice sheet and "spread southward explosively, briefly attaining a density sufficiently large to overkill much of their prey."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Others later proposed a "three-wave" migration over the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bering_Land_Bridge" title="Bering Land Bridge">\n        Bering Land Bridge\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These hypotheses remained the long-held view regarding the\n       <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_the_Americas" title="Settlement of the Americas">\n        settlement of the Americas\n       </a>\n       , a view challenged by more recent archaeological discoveries: the oldest archaeological sites in the Americas have been found in South America; sites in north-east Siberia report virtually no human presence there during the LGM; and most Clovis artefacts have been found in eastern North America along the Atlantic coast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Furthermore, colonisation models based on mtDNA,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/YDNA" title="YDNA">\n        yDNA\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AtDNA" title="AtDNA">\n        atDNA\n       </a>\n       data respectively support neither the "blitzkrieg" nor the "three-wave" hypotheses but they also deliver mutually ambiguous results. Contradictory data from archaeology and genetics will most likely deliver future hypotheses that will, eventually, confirm each other.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A proposed route across the Pacific to South America could explain early South American finds and another hypothesis proposes a northern path, through the Canadian Arctic and down the North American Atlantic coast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Early settlements across the Atlantic have been suggested by alternative theories, ranging from purely hypothetical to mostly disputed, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solutrean_hypothesis" title="Solutrean hypothesis">\n        Solutrean hypothesis\n       </a>\n       and some of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_trans-oceanic_contact_theories" title="Pre-Columbian trans-oceanic contact theories">\n        Pre-Columbian trans-oceanic contact theories\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Norse-world.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="666" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Norse-world.png/220px-Norse-world.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Norse-world.png/330px-Norse-world.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Norse-world.png/440px-Norse-world.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Norse-world.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Based on the medieval\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Sagas_of_Icelanders" title="Sagas of Icelanders">\n           \xc3\x8dslendingas\xc3\xb6gur\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         sagas, including the\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Greenland_saga" title="Greenland saga">\n           Gr\xc5\x93nlendinga saga\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         , this interpretative map of the "Norse World" shows that Norse knowledge of America and the Atlantic remained limited.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Norse_colonization_of_North_America" title="Norse colonization of North America">\n        Norse settlement\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">\n        Faroe Islands\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">\n        Iceland\n       </a>\n       began during the 9th and 10th centuries. A settlement on\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">\n        Greenland\n       </a>\n       was established before 1000\xc2\xa0CE, but contact with it was lost in 1409 and it was finally abandoned during the early\n       <a href="/wiki/Little_Ice_Age" title="Little Ice Age">\n        Little Ice Age\n       </a>\n       . This setback was caused by a range of factors: an unsustainable economy resulted in erosion and denudation, while conflicts with the local\n       <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">\n        Inuit\n       </a>\n       resulted in the failure to adapt their Arctic technologies; a colder climate resulted in starvation; and the colony got economically marginalized as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Plague" title="Great Plague">\n        Great Plague\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">\n        Barbary pirates\n       </a>\n       harvested its victims on Iceland in the 15th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Iceland was initially settled 865\xe2\x80\x93930\xc2\xa0CE following a warm period when winter temperatures hovered around 2\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (36\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) which made farming favorable at high latitudes. This did not last, however, and temperatures quickly dropped; at 1080\xc2\xa0CE summer temperatures had reached a maximum of 5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (41\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F). The\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Landn%C3%A1mab%C3%B3k" title="Landn\xc3\xa1mab\xc3\xb3k">\n         Landn\xc3\xa1mab\xc3\xb3k\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Book of Settlement\n       </i>\n       ) records disastrous famines during the first century of settlement\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 "men ate foxes and ravens" and "the old and helpless were killed and thrown over cliffs"\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 and by the early 1200s hay had to be abandoned for short-season crops such as barley.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Brendan#Possible_link_to_North_America" title="Brendan">\n        Brendan \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Possible link to North America\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Atlantic_World">\n        Atlantic World\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Atlantic World">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_world" title="Atlantic world">\n        Atlantic world\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_history" title="Atlantic history">\n        Atlantic history\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/220px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/330px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png/440px-Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Philip_II%27s_realms_in_1598.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A century after Columbus\' first voyage, large parts of the New World had been included into the\n         <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">\n          Spanish Empire\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">\n        Christopher Columbus\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">\n        discovered the Americas\n       </a>\n       in 1492 under Spanish flag.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chamb-184_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Chamb-184-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Six years later\n       <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">\n        Vasco da Gama\n       </a>\n       reached India under Portuguese flag, by navigating south around the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">\n        Cape of Good Hope\n       </a>\n       , thus proving that the Atlantic and Indian Oceans are connected. In 1500, in his voyage to India following Vasco da Gama,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedro_Alvares_Cabral" title="Pedro Alvares Cabral">\n        Pedro Alvares Cabral\n       </a>\n       reached Brazil, taken by the currents of the\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Gyre" title="South Atlantic Gyre">\n        South Atlantic Gyre\n       </a>\n       . Following these explorations, Spain and Portugal quickly\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Colonization of the Americas">\n        conquered and colonized\n       </a>\n       large territories in the New World and forced the Native American population into slavery in order to explore the vast quantities of silver and gold they found. Spain and Portugal monopolized this trade in order to keep other European nations out, but conflicting interests nevertheless led to a series of Spanish-Portuguese wars. A peace treaty mediated by the Pope divided the conquered territories into Spanish and Portuguese sectors while keeping other colonial powers away. England, France, and the Dutch Republic enviously watched the Spanish and Portuguese wealth grow and allied themselves with\n       <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Atlantic_World" title="Piracy in the Atlantic World">\n        pirates\n       </a>\n       such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Mainwaring" title="Henry Mainwaring">\n        Henry Mainwaring\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Exquemelin" title="Alexandre Exquemelin">\n        Alexandre Exquemelin\n       </a>\n       . They could explore the convoys leaving America because prevailing winds and currents made the transport of heavy metals slow and predictable.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chamb-184_64-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Chamb-184-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atlantic_slavetrade_estimates.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="731" data-file-width="1146" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Atlantic_slavetrade_estimates.png/220px-Atlantic_slavetrade_estimates.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Atlantic_slavetrade_estimates.png/330px-Atlantic_slavetrade_estimates.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Atlantic_slavetrade_estimates.png/440px-Atlantic_slavetrade_estimates.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atlantic_slavetrade_estimates.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Embarked and disembarked slaves in the\n         <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">\n          Atlantic slave trade\n         </a>\n         1525\xe2\x80\x931863 (first and last slave voyages)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the American colonies depredation, disease, and slavery quickly reduced the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">\n        indigenous American population\n       </a>\n       to the extent that the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">\n        Atlantic slave trade\n       </a>\n       had to be introduced to replace them\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 a trade that became norm and an integral part of the colonization. Between the 15th century and 1888, when\n       <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Brazil" title="Slavery in Brazil">\n        Brazil\n       </a>\n       became the last part of America to end slave trade, an estimated ten million Africans were exported as slaves, most of them destined for agricultural labour. The slave trade was officially abolished in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_British_Isles" title="Slavery in the British Isles">\n        British Empire\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       in 1808, and slavery itself was abolished in the British Empire in 1838 and in the U.S. in 1865 after the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        Civil War\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       From Columbus to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">\n        Industrial Revolution\n       </a>\n       Trans-Atlantic trade, including colonialism and slavery, became crucial for Western Europe. For European countries with a direct access to the Atlantic (including Britain, France, the Netherlands, Portugal, and Spain) 1500\xe2\x80\x931800 was a period of sustained growth during which these countries grew richer than those in Eastern Europe and Asia. Colonialism evolved as part of the Trans-Atlantic trade, but this trade also strengthened the position of merchant groups at the expense of monarchs. Growth was more rapid in non-absolutist countries, such as Britain and the Netherlands, and more limited in\n       <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">\n        absolutist monarchies\n       </a>\n       , such as Portugal, Spain, and France, where profit mostly or exclusively benefited the monarchy and its allies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Acem-p546_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Acem-p546-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Trans-Atlantic trade also resulted in an increasing urbanization: in European countries facing the Atlantic urbanization grew from 8% in 1300, 10.1% in 1500, to 24.5% in 1850; in other European countries from 10% in 1300, 11.4% in 1500, to 17% in 1850. Likewise, GDP doubled in Atlantic countries but rose by only 30% in the rest of Europe. By end of the 17th century the volume of the Trans-Atlantic trade had surpassed that of the Mediterranean trade.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Acem-p546_67-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Acem-p546-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_notable_crossings_of_the_Atlantic_Ocean" title="List of notable crossings of the Atlantic Ocean">\n        List of notable crossings of the Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The Atlantic has contributed significantly to the development and economy of surrounding countries. Besides major transatlantic transportation and communication routes, the Atlantic offers abundant petroleum deposits in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">\n        sedimentary rocks\n       </a>\n       of the continental shelves.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USN-2001_5-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USN-2001-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Atlantic harbors petroleum and gas fields, fish,\n       <a href="/wiki/Marine_mammal" title="Marine mammal">\n        marine mammals\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">\n        seals\n       </a>\n       and whales),\n       <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">\n        sand\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">\n        gravel\n       </a>\n       aggregates,\n       <a href="/wiki/Placer_deposit" title="Placer deposit">\n        placer deposits\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polymetallic_nodules" title="Polymetallic nodules">\n        polymetallic nodules\n       </a>\n       , and precious stones.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Gold deposits are a mile or two under water on the ocean floor, however the deposits are also encased in rock that must be mined through. Currently, there is no cost-effective way to mine or extract gold from the ocean to make a profit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Various international treaties attempt to reduce pollution caused by environmental threats such as oil spills,\n       <a href="/wiki/Marine_debris" title="Marine debris">\n        marine debris\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Incineration" title="Incineration">\n        incineration\n       </a>\n       of toxic wastes at sea.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USN-2001_5-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USN-2001-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fisheries">\n        Fisheries\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Fisheries">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">\n        shelves\n       </a>\n       of the Atlantic hosts one of the world\'s richest\n       <a href="/wiki/Wild_fisheries" title="Wild fisheries">\n        fishing resources\n       </a>\n       . The most productive areas include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Banks_of_Newfoundland" title="Grand Banks of Newfoundland">\n        Grand Banks of Newfoundland\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Scotian_Shelf" title="Scotian Shelf">\n        Scotian Shelf\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Georges_Bank" title="Georges Bank">\n        Georges Bank\n       </a>\n       off\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod" title="Cape Cod">\n        Cape Cod\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bahama_Banks" title="Bahama Banks">\n        Bahama Banks\n       </a>\n       , the waters around Iceland, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">\n        Irish Sea\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">\n        Bay of Fundy\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dogger_Bank" title="Dogger Bank">\n        Dogger Bank\n       </a>\n       of the North Sea, and the Falkland Banks.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USN-2001_5-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USN-2001-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Fisheries have, however, undergone significant changes since the 1950s and global catches can now be divided into three groups of which only two are observed in the Atlantic: fisheries in the Eastern Central and South-West Atlantic oscillate around a globally stable value, the rest of the Atlantic is in overall decline following historical peaks. The third group, "continuously increasing trend since 1950", is only found in the Indian Ocean and Western Pacific.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOA-2016-p39_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOA-2016-p39-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Northeast_Atlantic_bathymetry.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="323" data-file-width="413" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Northeast_Atlantic_bathymetry.png/220px-Northeast_Atlantic_bathymetry.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Northeast_Atlantic_bathymetry.png/330px-Northeast_Atlantic_bathymetry.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/Northeast_Atlantic_bathymetry.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Northeast_Atlantic_bathymetry.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Banks of the North-East Atlantic\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the North-East Atlantic total catches decreased between the mid-1970s and the 1990s and reached 8.7 million tons in 2013.\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_whiting" title="Blue whiting">\n        Blue whiting\n       </a>\n       reached a 2.4 million tons peak in 2004 but was down to 628,000 tons in 2013. Recovery plans for cod, sole, and plaice have reduced mortality in these species.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arctic_cod" title="Arctic cod">\n        Arctic cod\n       </a>\n       reached its lowest levels in the 1960s\xe2\x80\x931980s but is now recovered.\n       <a href="/wiki/Pollachius_virens" title="Pollachius virens">\n        Arctic saithe\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Haddock" title="Haddock">\n        haddock\n       </a>\n       are considered fully fished;\n       <a href="/wiki/Sand_eel" title="Sand eel">\n        Sand eel\n       </a>\n       is overfished as was\n       <a href="/wiki/Capelin" title="Capelin">\n        capelin\n       </a>\n       which has now recovered to fully fished. Limited data makes the state of\n       <a href="/wiki/Redfish" title="Redfish">\n        redfishes\n       </a>\n       and deep-water species difficult to assess but most likely they remain vulnerable to overfishing. Stocks of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_shrimp" title="Northern shrimp">\n        northern shrimp\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_lobster" title="Norwegian lobster">\n        Norwegian lobster\n       </a>\n       are in good condition. In the North-East Atlantic 21% of stocks are considered overfished.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOA-2016-p39_70-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOA-2016-p39-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:StLawrence_Gulf_bathymetry.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="505" data-file-width="820" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/StLawrence_Gulf_bathymetry.jpg/220px-StLawrence_Gulf_bathymetry.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/StLawrence_Gulf_bathymetry.jpg/330px-StLawrence_Gulf_bathymetry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/StLawrence_Gulf_bathymetry.jpg/440px-StLawrence_Gulf_bathymetry.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:StLawrence_Gulf_bathymetry.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Banks of the North-West Atlantic\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the North-West Atlantic landings have decreased from 4.2 million tons in the early 1970s to 1.9 million tons in 2013. During the 21th century some species have shown weak signs of recovery, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenland_halibut" title="Greenland halibut">\n        Greenland halibut\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Yellowtail_flounder" title="Yellowtail flounder">\n        yellowtail flounder\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_halibut" title="Atlantic halibut">\n        Atlantic halibut\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Haddock" title="Haddock">\n        haddock\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Spiny_dogfish" title="Spiny dogfish">\n        spiny dogfish\n       </a>\n       , while other stocks shown no such signs, including cod,\n       <a href="/wiki/Witch_(righteye_flounder)" title="Witch (righteye flounder)">\n        witch flounder\n       </a>\n       , and redfish. Stocks of invertebrates, in contrast, remain at record levels of abundance. 31% of stocks are overfished in the North-west Atlantic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOA-2016-p39_70-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOA-2016-p39-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Time_series_for_collapse_of_Atlantic_northwest_cod.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="837" data-file-width="1284" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Time_series_for_collapse_of_Atlantic_northwest_cod.png/220px-Time_series_for_collapse_of_Atlantic_northwest_cod.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Time_series_for_collapse_of_Atlantic_northwest_cod.png/330px-Time_series_for_collapse_of_Atlantic_northwest_cod.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Time_series_for_collapse_of_Atlantic_northwest_cod.png/440px-Time_series_for_collapse_of_Atlantic_northwest_cod.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Time_series_for_collapse_of_Atlantic_northwest_cod.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Capture of Atlantic north-west cod in million tons\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1497\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">\n        John Cabot\n       </a>\n       became the first to explore mainland North America and one of his major discoveries was the abundant resources of\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_cod" title="Atlantic cod">\n        Atlantic cod\n       </a>\n       off Newfoundland. Referred to as "Newfoundland Currency" this discovery supplied mankind with some 200\xc2\xa0million tons of fish over five centuries. In the late 19th and early 20th centuries new fisheries started to exploit\n       <a href="/wiki/Haddock" title="Haddock">\n        haddock\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mackerel" title="Mackerel">\n        mackerel\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lobster" title="Lobster">\n        lobster\n       </a>\n       . From the 1950s to the 1970s the introduction of European and Asian distant-water fleets in the area dramatically increased the fishing capacity and number of exploited species. It also expanded the exploited areas from near-shore to the open sea and to great depths to include deep-water species such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Sebastes" title="Sebastes">\n        redfish\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenland_halibut" title="Greenland halibut">\n        Greenland halibut\n       </a>\n       , witch flounder, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Grenadiers_(fish)" title="Grenadiers (fish)">\n        grenadiers\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">\n        Overfishing\n       </a>\n       in the area was recognised as early as the 1960s but, because this was occurring on\n       <a href="/wiki/International_waters" title="International waters">\n        international waters\n       </a>\n       , it took until the late 1970s before any attempts to regulate was made. In the early 1990s this finally resulted in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_Atlantic_northwest_cod_fishery" title="Collapse of the Atlantic northwest cod fishery">\n        collapse of the Atlantic northwest cod fishery\n       </a>\n       . The population of a number of deep-sea fishes also collapsed in the process, including\n       <a href="/wiki/American_plaice" title="American plaice">\n        American plaice\n       </a>\n       , redfish, and Greenland halibut, together with flounder and grenadier.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the Eastern Central Atlantic small\n       <a href="/wiki/Pelagic_fish" title="Pelagic fish">\n        pelagic fishes\n       </a>\n       constitute about 50% of landings with sardine reaching 0.6\xe2\x80\x931.0 million tons per year. Pelagic fish stocks are considered fully fishes or overfished, with sardines south of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Bojador" title="Cape Bojador">\n        Cape Bojador\n       </a>\n       the notable exception. Almost half of stocks are fished at biologically unsustainable levels. Total catches have been fluctuating since the 1970s; reaching 3.9 million tons in 2013 or slightly less than the peak production in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOA-2016-p39_70-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOA-2016-p39-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bahamas.A2001138.1550.250m.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3200" data-file-width="2400" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Bahamas.A2001138.1550.250m.jpg/170px-Bahamas.A2001138.1550.250m.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Bahamas.A2001138.1550.250m.jpg/255px-Bahamas.A2001138.1550.250m.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Bahamas.A2001138.1550.250m.jpg/340px-Bahamas.A2001138.1550.250m.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bahamas.A2001138.1550.250m.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Bahama_Banks" title="Bahama Banks">\n          Bahama Banks\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the Western Central Atlantic catches have been decreasing since 2000 and reached 1.3 million tons in 2013. The most important species in the area,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_menhaden" title="Gulf menhaden">\n        Gulf menhaden\n       </a>\n       , reached a million tons in the mid-1980s but only half a million tons in 2013 and is now considered fully fished.\n       <a href="/wiki/Round_sardinella" title="Round sardinella">\n        Round sardinella\n       </a>\n       was an important species in the 1990s but is now considered overfished.\n       <a href="/wiki/Grouper" title="Grouper">\n        Groupers\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lutjanidae" title="Lutjanidae">\n        snappers\n       </a>\n       are overfished and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_brown_shrimp" title="Northern brown shrimp">\n        northern brown shrimp\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_oyster" title="Eastern oyster">\n        American cupped oyster\n       </a>\n       are considered fully fished approaching overfished. 44% of stocks are being fished at unsustainable levels.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOA-2016-p39_70-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOA-2016-p39-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Agulhas_Bank_NOAA_ETOPO1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="417" data-file-width="703" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Agulhas_Bank_NOAA_ETOPO1.jpg/220px-Agulhas_Bank_NOAA_ETOPO1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Agulhas_Bank_NOAA_ETOPO1.jpg/330px-Agulhas_Bank_NOAA_ETOPO1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Agulhas_Bank_NOAA_ETOPO1.jpg/440px-Agulhas_Bank_NOAA_ETOPO1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Agulhas_Bank_NOAA_ETOPO1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Agulhas_Bank" title="Agulhas Bank">\n          Agulhas Bank\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the South-East Atlantic catches have decreased from 3.3 million tons in the early 1970s to 1.3 million tons in 2013.\n       <a href="/wiki/Horse_mackerel" title="Horse mackerel">\n        Horse mackerel\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hake" title="Hake">\n        hake\n       </a>\n       are the most important species, together representing almost half of the landings. Off South Africa and Namibia\n       <a href="/wiki/Merluccius_paradoxus" title="Merluccius paradoxus">\n        deep-water hake\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Merluccius_capensis" title="Merluccius capensis">\n        shallow-water Cape hake\n       </a>\n       have recovered to sustainable levels since regulations were introduced in 2006 and the states of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_African_pilchard" title="Southern African pilchard">\n        Southern African pilchard\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_anchovy" title="Southern African anchovy">\n        anchovy\n       </a>\n       have improved to fully fished in 2013.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOA-2016-p39_70-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOA-2016-p39-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the South-West Atlantic a peak was reached in the mid-1980s and catches now fluctuate between 1.7 and 2.6 million tons. The most important species, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Illex_argentinus" title="Illex argentinus">\n        Argentine shortfin squid\n       </a>\n       , which reached half a million tons in 2013 or half the peak value, is considered fully fished to overfished. Another important species was the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_sardinella" title="Brazilian sardinella">\n        Brazilian sardinella\n       </a>\n       , with a production of 100,000 tons in 2013 it is now considered overfished. Half the stocks in this area are being fished at unsustainable levels:\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Whitehead%E2%80%99s_round_herring&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Whitehead\xe2\x80\x99s round herring (page does not exist)">\n        Whitehead\xe2\x80\x99s round herring\n       </a>\n       has not yet reached fully fished but\n       <a href="/wiki/Cunene_horse_mackerel" title="Cunene horse mackerel">\n        Cunene horse mackerel\n       </a>\n       is overfished. The sea snail\n       <a href="/wiki/Haliotis_midae" title="Haliotis midae">\n        perlemoen abalone\n       </a>\n       is targeted by illegal fishing and remain overfished.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOA-2016-p39_70-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOA-2016-p39-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_fisheries#Atlantic_Ocean" title="Ocean fisheries">\n        Ocean fisheries \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fishing_down_the_food_web" title="Fishing down the food web">\n        Fishing down the food web\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">\n        Environmental issues\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nesocichla_eremita_-Inaccessible_Island,_British_overseas_territory-8_(3).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2543" data-file-width="3814" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Nesocichla_eremita_-Inaccessible_Island%2C_British_overseas_territory-8_%283%29.jpg/220px-Nesocichla_eremita_-Inaccessible_Island%2C_British_overseas_territory-8_%283%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Nesocichla_eremita_-Inaccessible_Island%2C_British_overseas_territory-8_%283%29.jpg/330px-Nesocichla_eremita_-Inaccessible_Island%2C_British_overseas_territory-8_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Nesocichla_eremita_-Inaccessible_Island%2C_British_overseas_territory-8_%283%29.jpg/440px-Nesocichla_eremita_-Inaccessible_Island%2C_British_overseas_territory-8_%283%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nesocichla_eremita_-Inaccessible_Island,_British_overseas_territory-8_(3).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Marine_debris" title="Marine debris">\n          Marine debris\n         </a>\n         strewn over the beaches of the South Atlantic\n         <a href="/wiki/Inaccessible_Island" title="Inaccessible Island">\n          Inaccessible Island\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Endangered marine species include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Manatee" title="Manatee">\n        manatee\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">\n        seals\n       </a>\n       , sea lions, turtles, and whales.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drift_net" title="Drift net">\n        Drift net\n       </a>\n       fishing can kill dolphins,\n       <a href="/wiki/Albatross" title="Albatross">\n        albatrosses\n       </a>\n       and other seabirds (\n       <a href="/wiki/Petrel" title="Petrel">\n        petrels\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Auk" title="Auk">\n        auks\n       </a>\n       ), hastening the fish stock decline and contributing to international disputes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Municipal pollution comes from the eastern United States, southern Brazil, and eastern Argentina;\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_pollution" title="Oil pollution">\n        oil pollution\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">\n        Caribbean Sea\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">\n        Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Maracaibo" title="Lake Maracaibo">\n        Lake Maracaibo\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">\n        Mediterranean Sea\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">\n        North Sea\n       </a>\n       ; and industrial waste and municipal sewage pollution in the Baltic Sea, North Sea, and Mediterranean Sea.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       North Atlantic hurricane activity has increased over past decades because of increased sea surface temperature (SST) at tropical latitudes, changes that can be attributed to either the natural\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Multidecadal_Oscillation" title="Atlantic Multidecadal Oscillation">\n        Atlantic Multidecadal Oscillation\n       </a>\n       (AMO) or to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anthropogenic_climate_change" title="Anthropogenic climate change">\n        anthropogenic climate change\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mann_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mann-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A 2005 report indicated that the Atlantic\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meridional_overturning_circulation" title="Meridional overturning circulation">\n        meridional overturning circulation\n       </a>\n       (AMOC) slowed down by 30% between 1957 and 2004.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       If the AMO were responsible for SST variability, the AMOC would have increased in strength, which is apparently not the case. Furthermore, it is clear from statistical analyses of annual tropical cyclones that these changes do not display multidecadal cyclicity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mann_73-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mann-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Therefore, these changes in SST must be caused by human activities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The ocean\n       <a href="/wiki/Mixed_layer" title="Mixed layer">\n        mixed layer\n       </a>\n       plays an important role heat storage over seasonal and decadal time-scales, whereas deeper layers are affected over millennia and has a heat capacity about 50 times that of the mixed layer. This heat uptake provides a time-lag for climate change but it also results in a thermal expansion of the oceans which contribute to sea-level rise. 21st century global warming will probably result in an\n       <a href="/wiki/Equilibrium_level" title="Equilibrium level">\n        equilibrium sea-level\n       </a>\n       rise five times greater than today, whilst melting of glaciers, including that of the Greenland ice-sheet, expected to have virtually no effect during the 21st century, will probably result in a sea-level rise of 3\xe2\x80\x936\xc2\xa0m over a millennium.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 7 June 2006, Florida\'s wildlife commission voted to take the manatee off the state\'s endangered species list. Some environmentalists worry that this could erode safeguards for the popular sea creature.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Marine_pollution" title="Marine pollution">\n        Marine pollution\n       </a>\n       is a generic term for the entry into the ocean of potentially hazardous chemicals or particles. The biggest culprits are rivers and with them many agriculture\n       <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">\n        fertilizer\n       </a>\n       chemicals as well as livestock and human waste. The excess of oxygen-depleting chemicals leads to\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypoxia_(environmental)" title="Hypoxia (environmental)">\n        hypoxia\n       </a>\n       and the creation of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Dead_zone_(ecology)" title="Dead zone (ecology)">\n        dead zone\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Marine_debris" title="Marine debris">\n        Marine debris\n       </a>\n       , which is also known as marine litter, describes human-created waste floating in a body of water. Oceanic debris tends to accumulate at the center of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oceanic_gyres" title="Oceanic gyres">\n        gyres\n       </a>\n       and coastlines, frequently washing aground where it is known as beach litter.\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_shipping" title="Environmental impact of shipping">\n        Environmental impact of shipping\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Shutdown_of_thermohaline_circulation" title="Shutdown of thermohaline circulation">\n        Shutdown of thermohaline circulation\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlantic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n       <ul </span>\n         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle">\n          <a href="/wiki/Portal:Geography" title="Portal:Geography">\n           Geography portal\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </li>\n        <li style="display:table-row">\n         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">\n
